        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heterostructure engineering is one of the most promising modification strategies toward improving sluggish kinetics for the anode of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we report a systemic investigation on the different types of heterostructure interfaces' effects of discharging products (Na2O, Na2S, Na2Se) on the rate performance.  First-principle calcns. reveal that the Na2S/Na2Se interface possesses the lowest diffusion energy barrier (0.39 eV) of Na among three kinds of interface structures (Na2O/Na2S, Na2O/Na2Se, and Na2S/Na2Se) due to its smallest recorded interface deformation, similar electronegativity, and lattice const.  The exptl. evidence confirms that the metal sulfide/metal selenide (SnS/SnSe2) hierarchical anode exhibits outstanding rate performance, where the normalized capacity at 10 A g-1 compared to 0.1 A g-1 is 45.6%.  The proposed design strategy in this work is helpful to design high rate performance anodes for advanced battery systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9lxbr-vNIRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGDXL5tAyiXw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered-Structure SbPO4/Reduced Graphene Oxide: An Advanced Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Chen, Shulin; Fu, Qiang; Sun, Yuanwei; Zhang, Yuchen; Lin, Na; Gao, Peng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of most promising alternatives to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage, due to the high abundance and low cost of Na in the earth.  However, the lack of advanced electrode materials greatly affects their applications.  Here, layered-structure SbPO4 is explored as an anode material for Na ion batteries in terms of SbPO4 nanorods on reduced graphene oxide (SbPO4/rGO).  In situ transmission electron microscopy images reveal the preferential expansion along the transverse direction of the nanorods upon the first discharging, which arises from the redn. of SbPO4 to Sb and the subsequent alloying of Sb as supported by in situ x-ray diffraction and selected area electron diffraction patterns. Its specific capacity at 5 A/g is 214 mAh/g in half cells or 134 mAh/g in full cells.                 10.1021/acs.nanolett.8b04468</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D19%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D538-544%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DC.%2BCui%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BWei%26author%3DM.%2BMao%26author%3DX.%2BLian%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BFan%26author%3DJ.%2BMa%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26title%3DAntimony%2BNanorod%2BEncapsulated%2Bin%2BCross-Linked%2BCarbon%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.8b04468&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.8b04468&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Antimony Nanorod Encapsulated in Cross-Linked Carbon for High-Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Chunyu; Xu, Jiantie; Zhang, Yiqiong; Wei, Zengxi; Mao, Minglei; Lian, Xin; Wang, Shuangyin; Yang, Chongyin; Fan, Xiulin; Ma, Jianmin; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">538-544</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony- (Sb) based materials have been considered as one of promising anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high theor. capacities and appropriate sodium inserting potentials.  So far, the reported energy d. and cycling stability of the Sb-based anodes for SIBs are quite limited and need to be significantly improved.  Here, we develop a novel Sb/C hybrid encapsulating the Sb nanorods into highly conductive N and S codoped carbon (Sb@(N, S-C)) frameworks.  As an anode for SIBs, the Sb@(N, S-C) hybrid maintains high reversible capacities of 621.1 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 150 cycles, and 390.8 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles.  At higher current densities of 2, 5, and 10 A g-1, the Sb@(N, S-C) hybrid also can display high reversible capacities of 534.4, 430.8, and 374.7 mAh g-1, resp.  Such impressive sodium storage properties are mainly attributed to the unique cross-linked carbon networks providing highly conductive frameworks for fast transfer of ions and electrons, alleviating the vol. expansion and preventing the agglomeration of Sb nanorods during the cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZsRX3dyx3q7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifxCmavOXYDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFCjtLnK&amp;md5=8e708a9d00ca59428b06d8c7bd5527e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201700522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoSe<sub>2</sub>-Covered N, P-Doped Carbon Nanosheets as a Long-Life and High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">22809</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">22818</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8TA09544B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D22809-22818%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DC.%2BKim%26author%3DI.%2BKim%26author%3DH.%2BKim%26author%3DM.%2BK.%2BSadan%26author%3DH.%2BYeo%26author%3DG.%2BCho%26author%3DJ.%2BAhn%26author%3DJ.%2BAhn%26author%3DH.%2BAhn%26title%3DA%2BSelf-Healing%2BSn%2BAnode%2Bwith%2Ban%2BUltra-Long%2BCycle%2BLife%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8TA09544B&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8TA09544B&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A self-healing Sn anode with an ultra-long cycle life for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Changhyeon; Kim, Icpyo; Kim, Huihun; Sadan, Milan K.; Yeo, Hyewon; Cho, Gyubong; Ahn, Jaepyoung; Ahn, Jouhyeon; Ahn, Hyojun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22809-22818</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For a next-generation sodium battery to replace lithium ion batteries, it is essential to develop an anode with a long cycle life and high rate.  Sn is considered to be an ideal candidate for the anode of sodium ion batteries.  Here, we report a Sn anode that exhibits ultra-long-term cycle stability with a high capacity of 554 mA h g-1 at 10C-rate for 5000 cycles.  The optimized cell configuration consists of 1,2-dimethoxyethane as the electrolyte, a double separator including a nanoporous membrane, and a Sn anode with MWCNT as a conductive additive.  Its capacity retention reaches up to 99.8% and its coulombic efficiency is near 100% for 5000 cycles.  Surprisingly, we have discovered that the Sn powder exhibits a self-healing phenomenon during cycling.  Sn is initially pulverized into a nanometer-sized powder, and then forms a three-dimensional porous coral-like structure in which ligament-shaped micrometer-sized Sn particles are connected with a low coordination no. by room temp. sintering.  The coral-like structure is mech. stable towards vol. change and elec. connected.  The self-healing structure and mechanism provide a direction for the design of other electrodes with alloying mechanisms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpCtOApZWvRj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifxCmavOXYDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitVams7%252FM&amp;md5=a5ed090d6ec86675e496fc5f9db17d2e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.02.024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhi, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanoparticles Encapsulated in Graphene Backboned Carbonaceous Foams as High-Performance Anodes for Lithium-ion and Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">232</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">240</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.02.024</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D22%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D232-240%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DB.%2BLuo%26author%3DT.%2BQiu%26author%3DD.%2BYe%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BZhi%26title%3DTin%2BNanoparticles%2BEncapsulated%2Bin%2BGraphene%2BBackboned%2BCarbonaceous%2BFoams%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BLithium-ion%2Band%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2016.02.024&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2016.02.024&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin nanoparticles encapsulated in graphene backboned carbonaceous foams as high-performance anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Bin; Qiu, Tengfei; Ye, Delai; Wang, Lianzhou; Zhi, Linjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">232-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new type of hierarchical tin@carbon composite composed of graphene carbonaceous matrix and well-confined tin nanoparticles with a typical size of ∼15 nm (denoted as F-G/Sn@C) is developed and investigated as anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion storage.  The two dimensional graphene backboned matrix not only acts as a confinement layer preventing the tin nanoparticles from aggregating during the material prepn., but also functions as a phys. barrier to buffer the vol. change effect during charge/discharge processes.  As a consequence, the composite demonstrates excellent rate performance and cycling stability for both Li-ion and Na-ion storage.  In particular, the F-G/Sn@C anode exhibits an impressive reversible capacity of 506 mAh g-1 even after 500 cycles and a high-rate capacity of 270 mAh g-1 even at 3200 mA g-1 for Li-ion storage.  Moreover, a reversible Na-ion storage capacity of 413 mAh g-1 with negligible fading is also achieved.  The remarkable electrochem. performance, together with the facile synthetic approach for large scale prodn., enables such material as a highly attractive tin-based anode for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXsgmx8FWKsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifxCmavOXYDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjt1Wlsbs%253D&amp;md5=de71d232cab95a81d764c84864d4920a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6702-6707</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small Sn nanodots (1-2 nm) were delicately encapsulated in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers through electrospinning and thermal treatment.  The size and content of Sn particles can be controlled by changing reaction conditions.  When evaluated as binder- and current collector-free anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries, Sn NDs@PNC nanofibers delivered a reversible capacity of 633 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More impressively, a capacity of 450 mA h g-1 even at 10 000 mA g-1 and 483 mA h g-1 over 1300 cycles at 2000 mA g-1 were achieved.  To our knowledge, this is the highest rate performance and cyclic stability of tin for Na storage.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of Sn NDs@PNC is attributed to the following: First, the ultra-small Sn NDs (1-2 nm) decreases the abs. strain and improve the utilization rate of active materials during sodiation/de-sodiation process; second, the uniform distribution of Sn NDs in the fibrous carbon matrix is an important factor to generate a balanced stress over the whole composite with maintaining the integrity of the electrode upon prolonged cycling; third, the 1D porous N-doped carbon frame can interlink into a 3D conductive network, which facilitates the electron and Na+ diffusion kinetics and buffers the large vol. fluctuation of Sn NDs and prevents their pulverization and aggregation.  Carbon fibers also serve as both current collector and conductive material - this avoids the common loss of electrochem. contact between the active materials and the current collector/conductive additives, and reduces the inactive wt. and vol. of cells thus improving the energy d.  This simple and scalable synthesis as well as the promising electrochem. performance encourages application of Sn-based materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnXAQ9MCRr0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifxCmavOXYDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ks77J&amp;md5=c6f2a6fad6ab6e844a9149e974f0edf1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201801662"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Porous Tin Created by Tuning the Redox Potential Acts as an Advanced Electrode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3376</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3381</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Porous Tin Created by Tuning the Redox Potential Acts as an Advanced Electrode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Liubin; Ni, Youxuan; Lei, Kaixiang; Dong, Huanhuan; Tian, Sen; Li, Fujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted significant research interest for large-scale elec. energy storage.  However, anodes with good rate capability and long cycle life are still lacking.  Here, a three-dimensional (3D) porous Sn on Cu foil (Sn/Cu) is prepd. by tuning the redox potential of Cu+/Cu with a ligand of thiourea to trigger the replacement reaction between Cu and Sn2+.  The as-synthesized Sn/Cu is used as an integrated porous electrode and can be directly applied as an advanced freestanding electrode for SIBs.  Such a unique structure can efficiently relieve the strain caused by sodiation/desodiation and benefit penetration of the electrolyte and diffusion of Na+.  This is a merit of its large reversible capacity of about 700 mAh g-1 at 2500 mA g-1 for 400 cycles.  A full battery of Sn/Cu//Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)3F2 is constructed, which presents a high energy d. of 311.7 Wh kg-1 and long lifespan of 200 cycles.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructures of solid electrolyte interphases and their consequences for microsized Sn anodes in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Jiaqiang; Guo, Xuyun; Du, Xiaoqiong; Lin, Xiuyi; Huang, Jian-Qiu; Tan, Hong; Zhu, Ye; Zhang, Biao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">There has been increasing evidence that ether-based electrolytes offer more stable anode performance in sodium ion batteries, even for microsized alloy electrodes which suffer huge vol. change upon charge/discharge cycling.  It is speculated that ether-based electrolytes may give rise to more robust solid electrolyte interphases (SEIs), but the detailed mechanism remains unknown, due to the structural complexity and the extremely vulnerable nature of SEIs.  In this work, we unveil the characteristic SEI structure at Sn electrode surfaces in both carbonate- and ether-based electrolytes.  We adopt cryogenic transmission electron microscopy to probe the pristine SEI structure, in combination with XPS and d. functional theory calcns.  An ultrathin SEI forms in the ether-based electrolyte, with amorphous particles dispersed in the polymer-like matrix.  This unique nanostructure exhibits superior mech. elasticity and renders anomalous stability against the large vol. change of alloy electrodes, as evidenced by both electrochem. measurement and at. force microscopy.  Our work unravels the causes for the superiority of ether-based electrolytes in sodium-ion batteries, and we expect the potential of such an optimized SEI to enable the application of high-capacity anodes such as microsized alloys.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoO-t0XJX45m7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1CKLARtZclQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte Engineering Enables High Stability and Capacity Alloying Anodes for Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Lin; Cao, Zhen; Wahyudi, Wandi; Zhang, Jiao; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Cheng, Yong; Wang, Limin; Cavallo, Luigi; Anthopoulos, Thomas; Sun, Yang-Kook; Alshareef, Husam N.; Ming, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">766-776</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of sodium and potassium ion batteries with greater energy d. is gaining great attention.  Although recently proposed alloying anodes (e.g., Sn and Bi) demonstrate much higher capacity than classic carbon anodes, their severe capacity fading hinders their practical applications.  The failure mechanism has traditionally been attributed to the large volumetric change and/or their fragile solid electrolyte interphase (SEI).  However, herein a completely new concept and approach are presented based on electrolyte engineering to stabilize alloying anodes.  This approach results in unprecedented high capacity (&gt; 650 mAh g-1) and stability (&gt; 500 cycles) of alloying anodes by simply tuning the electrolyte compns., without the need for nanostructural control and/or carbon modification.  It is confirmed that the cation solvation structure, particularly the type and location of the anions in the electrolyte, plays a crit. role in alloying anode stabilization.  A new anionic and alloying anode reaction model is presented showing that the root cause of the capacity fading in these alloys is dictated by the properties of the anions and not only the vol. change or fragile SEI effect.  Our model elucidates the failure mechanism in alloying anodes and provides a new guideline for electrolyte design that stabilizes alloying anodes in emerging mobile ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvlve8l8FFQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1CKLARtZclQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisFWrtbg%253D&amp;md5=1aa8da1f21de6c9b41d98d19e371bb88</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.7b01398"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stratford, J.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigating Sodium Storage Mechanisms in Tin Anodes: A Combined Pair Distribution Function Analysis, Density Functional Theory, and Solid-State NMR Approach</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stratford, Joshua M.; Mayo, Martin; Allan, Phoebe K.; Pecher, Oliver; Borkiewicz, Olaf J.; Wiaderek, Kamila M.; Chapman, Karena W.; Pickard, Chris J.; Morris, Andrew J.; Grey, Clare P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The alloying mechanism of high-capacity tin anodes for sodium-ion batteries is investigated using a combined theor. and exptl. approach.  Ab initio random structure searching (AIRSS) and high-throughput screening using a species-swap method provide insights into a range of possible sodium-tin structures.  These structures are linked to expts. using both av. and local structure probes in the form of operando pair distribution function anal., X-ray diffraction, and 23Na solid-state NMR (ssNMR), along with ex situ119Sn ssNMR.  Through this approach, structures are proposed for the previously unidentified cryst. and amorphous intermediates.  The first electrochem. process of sodium insertion into tin results in the conversion of cryst. tin into a layered structure consisting of mixed Na/Sn occupancy sites intercalated between planar hexagonal layers of Sn atoms (approx. stoichiometry NaSn3).  Following this, NaSn2, which is predicted to be thermodynamically stable by AIRSS, forms; this contains hexagonal layers closely related to NaSn3, but has no tin atoms between the layers.  NaSn2 is broken down into an amorphous phase of approx. compn. Na1.2Sn.  Reverse Monte Carlo refinements of an ab initio mol. dynamics model of this phase show that the predominant tin connectivity is chains.  Further reaction with sodium results in the formation of structures contg. Sn-Sn dumbbells, which interconvert through a solid-soln. mechanism.  These structures are based upon Na5-xSn2, with increasing occupancy of one of its sodium sites commensurate with the amt. of sodium added. ssNMR results indicate that the final product, Na15Sn4, can store addnl. sodium atoms as an off-stoichiometry compd. (Na15+xSn4) in a manner similar to Li15Si4.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoc38PHXMuXTLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1CKLARtZclQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXntFSks7g%253D&amp;md5=34090f61e8093b85cadf56e61baeb78a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201603212"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rousse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Foix, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dugas, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Corte, D.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High capacity group-15 alloy anodes for Na-ion batteries: Electrochemical and mechanical insights</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mortazavi, Majid; Ye, Qiongjie; Birbilis, Nick; Medhekar, Nikhil V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Group-15 elements P, As, Sb and Bi offer the prospect of serving as functional alloying elements for developing high-capacity alloy anodes for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Here the authors obtain concn.-dependent electrochem. properties of Na alloys with group-15 elements using 1st principles calcns.  Since Na intercalation in these alloys is accompanied by a substantial vol. expansion that can lead to mech. failure and loss of capacity, the authors have also obtained a full set of concn.-dependent elastic properties for a single crystal as well as a polycryst. microstructure.  Sodiation of these alloys results in their significant elastic softening by as large as 60%.  In contrast to the group-14 alloys that are also being explored as anodes of NIBs, the elastic softening in group-15 alloys varies in a nonmonotonic manner with Na concn., and more importantly, the max. degrdn. of elastic properties does not necessarily occur at full sodiation.  The authors' results provide crucial insights into the electrochem. and mech. response of these alloys to Na intercalation, thus contributing to the design of failure-resistant architectures of high capacity NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSJQsodyMFLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLGR4ZzJ4s9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVantrc%253D&amp;md5=e9f64d13e5651087f3170658a6061757</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.10.044"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mortazavi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shenoy, V.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Accurate description of the mech. behavior of cryst. Using first principles simulations, we have investigated the intrinsic elastic properties of cryst. Na-M (M = Sn, Pb, Si and Ge) phases obsd. during Na intercalation.  We have obtained the complete set of concn.-dependent anisotropic elastic consts. as well as the av. macroscopic elastic moduli of polycryst. structures.  We find that sodiation of pure M phases leads to a remarkable elastic softening that results in up to 75% deterioration of the elastic moduli.  Our anal. of the electronic charge distribution demonstrates that the elastic softening during sodiation originates from a transition to weaker ionic interat. bonding.  Our results highlight the significance of the concn. dependence of the elastic moduli for the anal. of deformation behavior of Na alloy anodes of Na-ion batteries during sodiation and desodiation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqO3F51b6yoBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLGR4ZzJ4s9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslKqsLbI&amp;md5=5c1bf716365f6f723758b268fada0a33</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1007/s10854-006-9016-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Phase-Field Model Coupled with Large Elasto-Plastic Deformation: Application to Lithiated Silicon Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, L.; Fan, F.; Hong, L.; Chen, J.; Ji, Y.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A phase-field model, accounting for large elasto-plastic deformation, is developed to study the evolution of phase, morphol. and stress in cryst. silicon (Si) electrodes upon lithium (Li) insertion.  The Li concn. profiles and deformation geometries are co-evolved by solving a set of coupled phase-field and mechanics equations using the finite element method.  The present phase-field model is validated in comparison with a non-linear concn.-dependent diffusion model of lithiation in Si electrodes.  It is shown that as the lithiation proceeds, the hoop stress changes from the initial compression to tension in the surface layer of the Si electrode, which may explain the surface cracking obsd. in expts.  The present phase-field model is generally applicable to high-capacity electrode systems undergoing both phase change and large elasto-plastic deformation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq77EFU7HzwLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLGR4ZzJ4s9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslahsb7K&amp;md5=8d1e2eacaeed81f83f246cf9d6a06f2d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/nn204476h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, S. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Size-Dependent Fracture of Silicon Nanoparticles During Lithiation</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1522</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1531</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Size-Dependent Fracture of Silicon Nanoparticles During Lithiation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xiao Hua; Zhong, Li; Huang, Shan; Mao, Scott X.; Zhu, Ting; Huang, Jian Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1522-1531</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithiation of individual silicon nanoparticles was studied in real time with in situ TEM.  A strong size dependence of fracture was discovered; i.e., there exists a crit. particle diam. of ∼150 nm, below which the particles neither cracked nor fractured upon 1st lithiation, and above which the particles initially formed surface cracks and then fractured due to lithiation-induced swelling.  The unexpected surface cracking arose owing to the buildup of large tensile hoop stress, which reversed the initial compression, in the surface layer.  The stress reversal was attributed to the unique mechanism of lithiation in cryst. Si, taking place by movement of a two-phase boundary between the inner core of pristine Si and the outer shell of amorphous Li-Si alloy.  While the resulting hoop tension tended to initiate surface cracks, the small-sized nanoparticles nevertheless averted fracture.  This is because the stored strain energy from electrochem. reactions was insufficient to drive crack propagation, as dictated by the interplay between the two length scales, i.e., particle diam. and crack size, that control the fracture.  These results are diametrically opposite to those obtained previously from single-phase modeling, which predicted only compressive hoop stress in the surface layer and thus crack initiation from the center in lithiated Si particles and wires.  The work provides direct evidence of the mech. robustness of small Si nanoparticles for applications in lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq7mT_29kDFu7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLGR4ZzJ4s9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivVWksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=7c5347ef8e51a00af47eb935de9a2176</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00690J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sha, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sn Nanoparticles@Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofiber Composites as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn nanoparticles@nitrogen-doped carbon nanofiber composites as high-performance anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sha, Mo; Zhang, Hui; Nie, Yuting; Nie, Kaiqi; Lv, Xiaoxin; Sun, Na; Xie, Xinkai; Ma, Yanyun; Sun, Xuhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted increasing attention as an important supplement or alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs) due to the abundance of sodium resources and its much lower cost.  A crit. issue and great challenge in current battery research for the extensive application of SIBs is the development of earth-abundant and high-performance electrode materials.  In various studies of these electrode materials, Sn-based nanocomposites have been identified as promising anodes for SIBs.  In this study, Sn nanoparticles on nitrogen-doped carbon nanofiber composites (Sn@NCNFs) have been synthesized by an electrostatic spinning technique and used as anodes for SIBs. Addnl., these Sn@NCNFs also show excellent high-rate cycling performance and can maintain a capacity of up to 390 mA h g-1 even at an extremely high rate of 1C for over 1000 cycles.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly stable (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene composite anode of sodium-ion batteries synthesized by oxygen plasma assisted milling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Deliang; Liu, Jiangwen; Li, Xiang; Hu, Renzong; Zeng, Meiqing; Yang, Lichun; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene ((SnOx-Sn)@FLG) composite has been synthesized by O plasma-assisted milling.  Owing to the synergistic effect of rapid plasma heating and ball mill grinding, SnOx (1≤ x ≤2) nanoparticles generated from the reaction of Sn with O are tightly wrapped by FLG nanosheets which are simultaneously exfoliated from expanded graphite, forming secondary micro granules.  Inside the granules, the small size of the SnOx nanoparticles enables the fast kinetics for Na+ transfer.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn based materials are promising anodes both in Li-ion batteries and Na-ion batteries due to their high theor. capacities (994 mA h g-1 for LIBs and 847 mA h g-1 for SIBs, resp.).  In order to improve the cycle performance, Sn/N-doped carbon microcage composites (Sn/NMCs) with Sn nanodots uniformly embedded inside the N-doped carbon microcages are synthesized through a simple spray drying process, followed by thermal treatment.  When used as electrodes, Sn/NMCs exhibit an initial reversible capacity of 780 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1, and maintain 472 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles in LIBs.  For Na-ion batteries, Sn/NMCs deliver an initial reversible capacity of 439 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and maintain 332 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles.  The remarkable electrochem. performance is mainly owing to the advanced structure of Sn/NMCs, which could be attributed to the pore-formation using NaCl, and the grain size inhibition of Sn using N-doped carbon.  Moreover, this prepn. method is accessible to scale up and can be extended to fabricate other electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqv5URF-QPBF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhvybYYkzkf2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXksV2lsbY%253D&amp;md5=607bc5f24c2c6a72573bb9b1ed0d487b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2016.07.001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous Carbon Nanocages Encapsulated with Tin Nanoparticles for High Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">180</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">190</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Yolk-Shell Sn@C Eggette-like Nanostructure: Application in Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Site; Wang, Ziming; Liu, Jun; Yang, LinYu; Guo, Yue; Cheng, Lizi; Lei, Ming; Wang, Wenjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Yolk-shell carbon encapsulated tin (Sn@C) eggette-like compds. (SCE) have been synthesized by a facile method.  The SCE structures consist of tin cores covered by carbon membrane networks with extra voids between the carbon shell and tin cores.  The novel nanoarchitectures exhibit high electrochem. performance in both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  As anodes for LIBs, the SCE electrodes exhibit a specific capacity of ∼850 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C (100 mA g-1) and high rate capability (∼450 mA h g-1 remains) at high current densities up to 5 C (5000 mA g-1).                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-Like CoSe2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Li, Weijie; Kang, Yong-Mook; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6728-6735</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchin-like CoSe2 assembled by nanorods was synthesized via simple solvothermal route and was 1st applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with ether-based electrolytes.  The CoSe2 delivers excellent sodiation and de-sodiation properties when using 1 M NaCF3SO3 in diethyleneglycol dimethylether as an electrolyte and cycling between 0.5 and 3.0 V.  A high discharge capacity of 0.410 A h g-1 is obtained at 1 A g-1 after 1800 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 98.6% calcd. from the 30th cycle.  Even at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g-1, the capacity still maintains 0.097 A h g-1.  The reaction mechanism of the as-prepd. CoSe2 is also studied.  At discharged 1.56 V, insertion reaction occurs, while 2 conversion reactions take place at the 2nd and 3rd plateaus around 0.98 and 0.65 V.  During the charge process, Co 1st reacts with Na2Se to form NaxCoSe2 and then turns back to CoSe2.  In addn. to Na/CoSe2 half cells, Na3V2(PO4)3/CoSe2 full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 was studied.  The full cell exhibits a reversible capacity of 0.380 Ah g-1.  This work enriches the possibilities for anode materials for SIBs with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpzIV0Nvfw2qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhvybYYkzkf2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1GhtLnM&amp;md5=5a3155a0784f8e8bcf04652fe8bd5e08</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201607469"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, G.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt-Doped FeS2 Nanospheres with Complete Solid Solubility as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Shin, Jeongyim; Hu, Zhe; Chou, Shu-Lei; Chen, Jun; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering that the high capacity, long-term cycle life, and high-rate capability of anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a bottleneck currently, a series of Co-doped FeS2 solid solns. with different Co contents were prepd. by a facile solvothermal method, and for the first time their Na-storage properties were investigated.  The optimized Co0.5Fe0.5S2 (Fe0.5) has discharge capacities of 0.220 Ah g-1 after 5000 cycles at 2 A g-1 and 0.172 Ah g-1 even at 20 A g-1 with compatible ether-based electrolyte in a voltage window of 0.8-2.9 V.  The Fe0.5 sample transforms to layered NaxCo0.5Fe0.5S2 by initial activation, and the layered structure is maintained during following cycles.  The redox reactions of NaxCo0.5Fe0.5S2 are dominated by pseudocapacitive behavior, leading to fast Na+ insertion/extn. and durable cycle life.  A Na3V2(PO4)3/Fe0.5 full cell was assembled, delivering an initial capacity of 0.340 Ah g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqARcXONZc757Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrG8PLTEmdVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFWntbvL&amp;md5=2d6d2579cfa2e3270c7a3b6fee44c500</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201500196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">FeSe<sub>2</sub> Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeSe2 Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Hu, Zhe; Liu, Xue; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries. <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible and Binder-Free Electrodes of Sb/rGO and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/rGO Nanocomposites for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3822</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3829</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.201500783</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D3822-3829%26journal%3DSmall%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DC.%2BChen%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26author%3DX.%2BHu%26title%3DFlexible%2Band%2BBinder-Free%2BElectrodes%2Bof%2BSb%252FrGO%2Band%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FrGO%2BNanocomposites%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.201500783&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.201500783&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible and Binder-Free Electrodes of Sb/rGO and Na3V2(PO4)3/rGO Nanocomposites for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wei; Liu, Yangtao; Chen, Chaoji; Li, Zhen; Huang, Yunhui; Hu, Xianluo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">31</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3822-3829</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible power sources showed great promise in next-generation bendable, implantable, and wearable electronic systems.  Here, flexible and binder-free electrodes of Na3V2(PO4)3/reduced graphene oxide (NVP/rGO) and Sb/rGO nanocomposites for Na-ion batteries are reported.  The Sb/rGO and NVP/rGO paper electrodes with high flexibility and tailorability can be easily fabricated.  Sb and NVP nanoparticles are embedded homogeneously in the interconnected framework of rGO nanosheets, which provides structurally stable hosts for Na-ion intercalation and deintercalation.  The NVP/rGO paper-like cathode delivers a reversible capacity of 113 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and high capacity retention of ≈96.6% after 120 cycles.  The Sb/rGO paper-like anode gives a highly reversible capacity of 612 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, an excellent rate capacity up to 30 C, and a good cycle performance.  Also, the Na-ion full cell of NVP/rGO//Sb/rGO was fabricated, delivering a highly reversible capacity of ≈400 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 charge/discharge cycles.  This work may provide promising electrode candidates for developing next-generation energy-storage devices with high capacity and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqEuCL3VQtFtbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrG8PLTEmdVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFCltrw%253D&amp;md5=c6e885e922194d560b18ff20c7794ae7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201505918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Walled Sb@TiO<sub>2-x</sub> Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4126</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4133</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201505918</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D4126-4133%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DN.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BBai%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26title%3DDouble-Walled%2BSb%2540TiO2-x%2BNanotubes%2Bas%2Ba%2BSuperior%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BUltralong-Lifespan%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2Band%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201505918&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201505918&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Walled Sb@TiO2-x Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Bai, Zhongchao; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4126-4133</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, double-walled cryst. Sb@amorphous TiO2-x nanotubes are synthesized by the calcination of Sb2S3@TiO2 nanorods in Ar/H2 produced by the hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate (TBOT) on Sb2S3 nanorods.  The formation of the double-walled structures could be assigned to the facile redn. of Sb2S3 and the strong interaction of Sb to TiO2.  Such a structure accommodates the vol. variation upon cycling well, then keeps the structure stable.  Meanwhile, this calcination in Ar/H2 also generates a lot of oxygen vacancies in the shell, supported by Ti3+ species in XPS spectra.  They would enhance the charge-transfer kinetics, particularly at the interface.  Thus, the double-walled nanotubes show excellent electrochem. performance as an anode material in the lithium-ion batteries and in sodium-ion batteries, both of which are on the top of the reported list.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrrdrYefF6qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrG8PLTEmdVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjtlKms7Y%253D&amp;md5=0bb077f676824aae644f1f5f12368294</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA03434B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Uniformly-Distributed Sb Nanoparticles in Ionic Liquid-Derived Nitrogen-Enriched Carbon for Highly Reversible Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13411</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13420</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA03434B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D13411-13420%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DX.%2BXu%26author%3DZ.%2BDou%26author%3DE.%2BGu%26author%3DL.%2BSi%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BBao%26title%3DUniformly-Distributed%2BSb%2BNanoparticles%2Bin%2BIonic%2BLiquid-Derived%2BNitrogen-Enriched%2BCarbon%2Bfor%2BHighly%2BReversible%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7TA03434B&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7TA03434B&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniformly-distributed Sb nanoparticles in ionic liquid-derived nitrogen-enriched carbon for highly reversible sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xin; Dou, Zhifeng; Gu, Erlong; Si, Ling; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13411-13420</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antinomy has received considerable attention as one of the most promising anode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity and suitable working voltage.  However, the large vol. change of Sb during the alloying/dealloying process causes poor cycling stability and low rate capability, which hinder its practical application.  Here, the authors substantially enhance the Na storage performance of Sb by binding Sb nanoparticles in ionic liq.-derived N-enriched C (Sb@NC) via pyrolysis of an SbCl3/1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium dicyanamide mixt.  The Sb@NC composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 440 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, superior rate performance of 285 and 237 mA h g-1 at the high current densities of 2 and 5 A g-1, resp., and greatly improved cycle life of 328 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 100 A g-1 after 300 cycles in the half cell of SIBs.  In the full cell, the energy d. of Sb@NC//Na3V2(PO4)3/C is ∼147 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 50 W kg-1.  Even at 2.37 kW kg-1, an energy d. of ∼65 W h kg-1 is still retained.  The remarkably improved electrochem. performance could be assigned to the synergistic effect of nanoscale size, uniform distribution, and chem. coupling effect between Sb and ionic liq.-derived N-enriched C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqodGGRdGl-4rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrG8PLTEmdVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXosVCltrg%253D&amp;md5=58676af0e3ee4eb633c74aea69719a47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b12242"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Binding Sb Nanospheres on Graphene via Oxygen Bonds as Superior Anode for Ultrafast Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wan, Fang; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Zhang, Xiao-Hua; Zhang, Jing-Ping; Sun, Hai-Zhu; Yan, Qingyu; Han, Dong-Xue; Niu, Li; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7790-7799</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene incorporation should be one effective strategy to develop advanced electrode materials for a sodium-ion battery (SIB).  Herein, the micro/nanostructural Sb/graphene composite (Sb-O-G) is successfully prepd. with the uniform Sb nanospheres (∼100 nm) bound on the graphene via oxygen bonds.  It is revealed that the in-situ-constructed oxygen bonds play a significant role on enhancing Na-storage properties, esp. the ultrafast charge/discharge capability.  The oxygen-bond-enhanced Sb-O-G composite can deliver a high capacity of 220 mAh/g at an ultrahigh c.d. of 12 A/g, which is obviously superior to the similar Sb/G composite (130 mAh/g at 10 A/g) just without Sb-O-C bonds.  It also exhibits the highest Na-storage capacity compared to Sb/G and pure Sb nanoparticles as well as the best cycling performance.  More importantly, this Sb-O-G anode achieves ultrafast (120 C) energy storage in SIB full cells, which have already been shown to power a 26-bulb array and calculator.  All of these superior performances originate from the structural stability of Sb-O-C bonds during Na uptake/release, which has been verified by ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopies and IR spectroscopies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAWqDAYuZl6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUKZf5uIUmPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjvFylur8%253D&amp;md5=20ff4444ec296955ad0cbb06a02dfbef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201904771"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bu, X.
