        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi has emerged as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), owing to its high capacity and suitable operating potential.  However, large vol. changes during alloying/dealloying processes lead to poor cycling performance.  Here, Bi nanoparticle@C (Bi@C) composite is prepd. via a facile annealing method using a com. coordination compd. precursor of Bi citrate.  The composite has a uniform structure with Bi nanoparticles embedded within a C framework.  The nanosized structure ensures a fast kinetics and efficient alleviation of stress/strain caused by the vol. change, and the resilient and conductive C matrix provides an interconnected electron transportation pathway.  The Bi@C composite delivers outstanding Na-storage performance with an ultralong cycle life of 30,000 cycles at a high c.d. of 8 A/g and an excellent rate capability of 71% capacity retention at an ultrahigh current rate of 60 A/g.  Even at a high mass loading of 11.5 mg/cm2, a stable reversible capacity of 280 mAh/g can be obtained after 200 cycles.  Full SIBs by pairing with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode demonstrates superior performance.  Combining the facile synthesis and the com. precursor, the exceptional performance makes the Bi@C composite very promising for practical large-scale applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphFbJVR5Fy-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUKZf5uIUmPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFaks7zJ&amp;md5=2ab88019326b5ea2f446f861c305a41d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b00818"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface Modification of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> by Nitrogen and Sulfur Dual-Doped Carbon Layer with Advanced Sodium Storage Property</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13151</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13162</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.7b00818</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D13151-13162%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DX.%2BLiang%26author%3DX.%2BOu%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DQ.%2BPan%26author%3DX.%2BXiong%26author%3DR.%2BHu%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DM.%2BLiu%26title%3DSurface%2BModification%2Bof%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2Bby%2BNitrogen%2Band%2BSulfur%2BDual-Doped%2BCarbon%2BLayer%2Bwith%2BAdvanced%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BProperty%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.7b00818&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c00489&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.7b00818&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface Modification of Na3V2(PO4)3 by Nitrogen and Sulfur Dual-Doped Carbon Layer with Advanced Sodium Storage Property</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Xinghui; Ou, Xing; Zheng, Fenghua; Pan, Qichang; Xiong, Xunhui; Hu, Renzong; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13151-13162</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped carbon layer wrapped Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles (NVP@NSC) have been successfully fabricated by the facile solid-state method.  In this hierarchical structure, the Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles are well dispersed and closely coated by nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped carbon layer, constructing an effective and interconnected conducting network to reduce the internal resistance.  Furthermore, the uniform coating layers alleviate the agglomeration of Na3V2(PO4)3 as well as mitigate the side reaction between electrode and electrolyte.  Because of the excellent electron transfer mutually enhancing sodium diffusion for this extraordinary structure, the NVP@NSC composite delivers an impressive discharge capacity of 113.0 mAh g-1 at 1 C and shows a capacity retention of 82.1% after 5000 cycles at an ultrahigh rate of 50 C, suggesting the remarkable rate capability and long cyclicity.  Surprisingly, a reversible capacity of 91.1 mAh g-1 is maintained after 1000 cycles at 5 C under the elevated temp. of 55 °C.  The approach of nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 provides an effective and promising strategy to enhance the ultrahigh rate and ultralong life property of cathode, which can be used for large-scale com. prodn. in sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0gNMT4Ra6KrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUKZf5uIUmPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXltVSkt7g%253D&amp;md5=0df9650b3f37a70feb1012492856807f</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da85e18cf1b325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span class="sr-only">close</span></button><p>Article Views             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion battery (SIB) as one of the most promising large-scale energy storage devices has drawn great attention in recent years.  However, the development of SIBs is limited by the lacking of proper anodes with long cycling life-spans and large reversible capacities.  Here the authors present rational synthesis of Rayleigh instability-induced Bi nanorods encapsulated in N-doped C nanotubes (Bi@N-C) using Bi2S3 nanobelts as the template for high-performance SIB.  The Bi@N-C electrode delivers superior Na storage performance in half cells, including a high specific capacity (410 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1), long cycling lifespan (1000 cycles), and superior rate capability (368 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1).  When coupled with homemade Na3V2(PO4)3/C in full cells, this electrode also exhibits excellent performances with high power d. of 1190 W kg-1 and energy d. of 119 W h kg-1total.  The exceptional performance of Bi@N-C is ascribed to the unique nanorod@nanotube structure, which can accommodate vol. expansion of Bi during cycling and stabilize the solid electrolyte interphase layer and improve the electronic cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqxgGXYh1o70rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWf9MRUcXBAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXisFyiurw%253D&amp;md5=2f8d2bb8360b528aa191fffd58072883</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kundu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Talaie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duffort, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nazar, L.                 10.1021/acsenergylett.8b00762</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">β-SnSb for sodium ion battery anodes: phase transformations responsible for enhanced cycling stability revealed by in situ TEM</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Hezhen; Tan, Xuehai; Luber, Erik J.; Olsen, Brian C.; Kalisvaart, W. Peter; Jungjohann, Katherine L.; Mitlin, David; Buriak, Jillian M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1670-1676</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2380-8195</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">β-SnSb is known to be a highly stable anode for sodium ion batteries during cycling, but its sodiation-desodiation alloying reactions are poorly understood.  Combining in situ TEM with electroanal. methods, the authors demonstrate that β-SnSb forms Na3Sb and Na15Sn4 in sequence upon sodiation and re-forms as β-SnSb upon desodiation.  The neg. enthalpy of mixing for Sn and Sb is sufficient to cause sequentially deposited bilayers of Sn/Sb to transform into β-SnSb, resulting in comparable cycling stability.  The good cycling stability of β-SnSb results from the complex two-phase amorphous-nanocryst. microstructure in the partially charged-discharged states, as well as the intrinsic mech. toughness of the β phase.  Per the in situ TEM results, the sequential phase transformation shows minimal fracturing of the β-SnSb, indicating facile buffering of stresses.  Extensively cycled specimens eventually show cryst. Sn phase segregation, which may be the source of the ultimate capacity fade in the alloy and bilayers.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrS2jnkbSkBQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWf9MRUcXBAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFGlsLfM&amp;md5=aeb83fa206cc39d9e748441f69f3b441</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C8EE01023D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress on Sodium Ion Batteries: Potential High-Performance Anodes</span>. <i>Energy Environ.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to massively growing demand arising from energy storage systems, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been recognized as the most attractive alternative to the current commercialized lithium ion batteries (LIBs) owing to the wide availability and accessibility of sodium.  Unfortunately, the low energy d., inferior power d. and poor cycle life are still the main issues for SIBs in the current drive to push the entire technol. forward to meet the benchmark requirements for commercialization.  Over the past few years, tremendous efforts have been devoted to improving the performance of SIBs, in terms of higher energy d. and longer cycling lifespans, by optimizing the electrode structure or the electrolyte compn.  In particular, among the established anode systems, those materials, such as metals/alloys, phosphorus/phosphides, and metal oxides/sulfides/selenides, that typically deliver high theor. sodium-storage capacities have received growing interest and achieved significant progress.  Although some review articles on electrodes for SIBs have been published already, many new reports on these anode materials are constantly emerging, with more promising electrochem. performance achieved via novel structural design, surface modification, electrochem. performance testing techniques, etc.  So, we herein summarize the most recent developments on these high-performance anode materials for SIBs in this review.  Furthermore, the different reaction mechanisms, the challenges assocd. with these materials, and effective approaches to enhance performance are discussed.  The prospects for future high-energy anodes in SIBs are also discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQBTNlAIykC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWf9MRUcXBAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlOjt7jK&amp;md5=e4580fd3c5fcf8eb8cfa08a8dc758f49</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c03432"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gentle, I.                         rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomimetic Sn4P3 Anchored on Carbon Nanotubes as an Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ran, Lingbing; Luo, Bin; Gentle, Ian R.; Lin, Tongen; Sun, Qiang; Li, Ming; Rana, Md Masud; Wang, Lianzhou; Knibbe, Ruth</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, Sn4P3 has emerged as a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to the high specific capacity.  However, the use of Sn4P3 has been impeded by capacity fade and an inferior rate performance.  Herein, a biomimetic heterostructure is reported by using a simple hydrothermal reaction followed by thermal treatment.  This bottlebrush-like structure consists of a stem-like carbon nanotube (CNT) as the electron expressway and mech. support; fructus-like Sn4P3 nanoparticles as the active material; and the permeable stoma-like thin carbon coating as the buffer layer.  Having benefited from the biomimetic structure, a superior electrochem. performance is obtained in the SIBs.  It exhibits a high capacity of 742 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles at 0.2C, and superior rate performance with 449 mA h g-1 at 2C after 500 cycles.  Moreover, the sodium storage mechanism is confirmed by cyclic voltammetry and ex situ X-ray diffraction and transmission electron microscopy.  In situ electrochem. impedance spectroscopy was adopted to analyze the reaction dynamics.  This research represents a further step toward figuring out the inferior electrochem. performance of other metal phosphide materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqi0vlL0Pw9D7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWf9MRUcXBAA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Heterostructure engineering is one of the most promising modification strategies toward improving sluggish kinetics for the anode of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we report a systemic investigation on the different types of heterostructure interfaces' effects of discharging products (Na2O, Na2S, Na2Se) on the rate performance.  First-principle calcns. reveal that the Na2S/Na2Se interface possesses the lowest diffusion energy barrier (0.39 eV) of Na among three kinds of interface structures (Na2O/Na2S, Na2O/Na2Se, and Na2S/Na2Se) due to its smallest recorded interface deformation, similar electronegativity, and lattice const.  The exptl. evidence confirms that the metal sulfide/metal selenide (SnS/SnSe2) hierarchical anode exhibits outstanding rate performance, where the normalized capacity at 10 A g-1 compared to 0.1 A g-1 is 45.6%.  The proposed design strategy in this work is helpful to design high rate performance anodes for advanced battery systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9lxbr-vNIRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWf9MRUcXBAA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of most promising alternatives to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage, due to the high abundance and low cost of Na in the earth.  However, the lack of advanced electrode materials greatly affects their applications.  Here, layered-structure SbPO4 is explored as an anode material for Na ion batteries in terms of SbPO4 nanorods on reduced graphene oxide (SbPO4/rGO).  In situ transmission electron microscopy images reveal the preferential expansion along the transverse direction of the nanorods upon the first discharging, which arises from the redn. of SbPO4 to Sb and the subsequent alloying of Sb as supported by in situ x-ray diffraction and selected area electron diffraction patterns.  SbPO4/rGO exhibits a capacity retention of 99% after 100 cycles at 0.5 A/g both in half cells and in full cells.  Its specific capacity at 5 A/g is 214 mAh/g in half cells or 134 mAh/g in full cells.  The energy d. of the full cells at 1.2 KW/Kgtotal is still 99.8 Wh/Kgtotal, very promising as an advanced electrode material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQXjyU3XiANLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDcteH_uZCCA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony- (Sb) based materials have been considered as one of promising anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high theor. capacities and appropriate sodium inserting potentials.  So far, the reported energy d. and cycling stability of the Sb-based anodes for SIBs are quite limited and need to be significantly improved.  Here, we develop a novel Sb/C hybrid encapsulating the Sb nanorods into highly conductive N and S codoped carbon (Sb@(N, S-C)) frameworks.  As an anode for SIBs, the Sb@(N, S-C) hybrid maintains high reversible capacities of 621.1 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 150 cycles, and 390.8 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles.  At higher current densities of 2, 5, and 10 A g-1, the Sb@(N, S-C) hybrid also can display high reversible capacities of 534.4, 430.8, and 374.7 mAh g-1, resp.  Such impressive sodium storage properties are mainly attributed to the unique cross-linked carbon networks providing highly conductive frameworks for fast transfer of ions and electrons, alleviating the vol. expansion and preventing the agglomeration of Sb nanorods during the cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZsRX3dyx3q7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDcteH_uZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFCjtLnK&amp;md5=8e708a9d00ca59428b06d8c7bd5527e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201700522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoSe<sub>2</sub>-Covered N, P-Doped Carbon Nanosheets as a Long-Life and High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A self-healing Sn anode with an ultra-long cycle life for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Changhyeon; Kim, Icpyo; Kim, Huihun; Sadan, Milan K.; Yeo, Hyewon; Cho, Gyubong; Ahn, Jaepyoung; Ahn, Jouhyeon; Ahn, Hyojun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For a next-generation sodium battery to replace lithium ion batteries, it is essential to develop an anode with a long cycle life and high rate.  Sn is considered to be an ideal candidate for the anode of sodium ion batteries.  Here, we report a Sn anode that exhibits ultra-long-term cycle stability with a high capacity of 554 mA h g-1 at 10C-rate for 5000 cycles.  The optimized cell configuration consists of 1,2-dimethoxyethane as the electrolyte, a double separator including a nanoporous membrane, and a Sn anode with MWCNT as a conductive additive.  Its capacity retention reaches up to 99.8% and its coulombic efficiency is near 100% for 5000 cycles.  Surprisingly, we have discovered that the Sn powder exhibits a self-healing phenomenon during cycling.  Sn is initially pulverized into a nanometer-sized powder, and then forms a three-dimensional porous coral-like structure in which ligament-shaped micrometer-sized Sn particles are connected with a low coordination no. by room temp. sintering.  The coral-like structure is mech. stable towards vol. change and elec. connected.  The self-healing structure and mechanism provide a direction for the design of other electrodes with alloying mechanisms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpCtOApZWvRj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDcteH_uZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitVams7%252FM&amp;md5=a5ed090d6ec86675e496fc5f9db17d2e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.02.024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhi, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanoparticles Encapsulated in Graphene Backboned Carbonaceous Foams as High-Performance Anodes for Lithium-ion and Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">232</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">240</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin nanoparticles encapsulated in graphene backboned carbonaceous foams as high-performance anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Bin; Qiu, Tengfei; Ye, Delai; Wang, Lianzhou; Zhi, Linjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new type of hierarchical tin@carbon composite composed of graphene carbonaceous matrix and well-confined tin nanoparticles with a typical size of ∼15 nm (denoted as F-G/Sn@C) is developed and investigated as anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion storage.  The two dimensional graphene backboned matrix not only acts as a confinement layer preventing the tin nanoparticles from aggregating during the material prepn., but also functions as a phys. barrier to buffer the vol. change effect during charge/discharge processes.  As a consequence, the composite demonstrates excellent rate performance and cycling stability for both Li-ion and Na-ion storage.  In particular, the F-G/Sn@C anode exhibits an impressive reversible capacity of 506 mAh g-1 even after 500 cycles and a high-rate capacity of 270 mAh g-1 even at 3200 mA g-1 for Li-ion storage.  Moreover, a reversible Na-ion storage capacity of 413 mAh g-1 with negligible fading is also achieved.  The remarkable electrochem. performance, together with the facile synthetic approach for large scale prodn., enables such material as a highly attractive tin-based anode for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXsgmx8FWKsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDcteH_uZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjt1Wlsbs%253D&amp;md5=de71d232cab95a81d764c84864d4920a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/adma.201503015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6702-6707</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small Sn nanodots (1-2 nm) were delicately encapsulated in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers through electrospinning and thermal treatment.  The size and content of Sn particles can be controlled by changing reaction conditions.  When evaluated as binder- and current collector-free anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries, Sn NDs@PNC nanofibers delivered a reversible capacity of 633 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More impressively, a capacity of 450 mA h g-1 even at 10 000 mA g-1 and 483 mA h g-1 over 1300 cycles at 2000 mA g-1 were achieved.  To our knowledge, this is the highest rate performance and cyclic stability of tin for Na storage.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of Sn NDs@PNC is attributed to the following: First, the ultra-small Sn NDs (1-2 nm) decreases the abs. strain and improve the utilization rate of active materials during sodiation/de-sodiation process; second, the uniform distribution of Sn NDs in the fibrous carbon matrix is an important factor to generate a balanced stress over the whole composite with maintaining the integrity of the electrode upon prolonged cycling; third, the 1D porous N-doped carbon frame can interlink into a 3D conductive network, which facilitates the electron and Na+ diffusion kinetics and buffers the large vol. fluctuation of Sn NDs and prevents their pulverization and aggregation.  Carbon fibers also serve as both current collector and conductive material - this avoids the common loss of electrochem. contact between the active materials and the current collector/conductive additives, and reduces the inactive wt. and vol. of cells thus improving the energy d.  This simple and scalable synthesis as well as the promising electrochem. performance encourages application of Sn-based materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnXAQ9MCRr0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDcteH_uZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ks77J&amp;md5=c6f2a6fad6ab6e844a9149e974f0edf1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201801662"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Porous Tin Created by Tuning the Redox Potential Acts as an Advanced Electrode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3376</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3381</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted significant research interest for large-scale elec. energy storage.  However, anodes with good rate capability and long cycle life are still lacking.  Here, a three-dimensional (3D) porous Sn on Cu foil (Sn/Cu) is prepd. by tuning the redox potential of Cu+/Cu with a ligand of thiourea to trigger the replacement reaction between Cu and Sn2+.  The as-synthesized Sn/Cu is used as an integrated porous electrode and can be directly applied as an advanced freestanding electrode for SIBs.  Such a unique structure can efficiently relieve the strain caused by sodiation/desodiation and benefit penetration of the electrolyte and diffusion of Na+.  This is a merit of its large reversible capacity of about 700 mAh g-1 at 2500 mA g-1 for 400 cycles.  A full battery of Sn/Cu//Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)3F2 is constructed, which presents a high energy d. of 311.7 Wh kg-1 and long lifespan of 200 cycles.  This facile synthesis strategy and good electrochem. performance will encourage more investigations into structure design of functional materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoY98iPh1Q6v7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDcteH_uZCCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhs1GksbjM&amp;md5=4a5ce72522e05f3c0ca3f01d3550e756</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C8EE03632B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructures of Solid Electrolyte Interphases and Their Consequences for Microsized Sn Anodes in Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                 10.1039/C8EE03632B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructures of solid electrolyte interphases and their consequences for microsized Sn anodes in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Jiaqiang; Guo, Xuyun; Du, Xiaoqiong; Lin, Xiuyi; Huang, Jian-Qiu; Tan, Hong; Zhu, Ye; Zhang, Biao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">There has been increasing evidence that ether-based electrolytes offer more stable anode performance in sodium ion batteries, even for microsized alloy electrodes which suffer huge vol. change upon charge/discharge cycling.  It is speculated that ether-based electrolytes may give rise to more robust solid electrolyte interphases (SEIs), but the detailed mechanism remains unknown, due to the structural complexity and the extremely vulnerable nature of SEIs.  In this work, we unveil the characteristic SEI structure at Sn electrode surfaces in both carbonate- and ether-based electrolytes.  We adopt cryogenic transmission electron microscopy to probe the pristine SEI structure, in combination with XPS and d. functional theory calcns.  An ultrathin SEI forms in the ether-based electrolyte, with amorphous particles dispersed in the polymer-like matrix.  This unique nanostructure exhibits superior mech. elasticity and renders anomalous stability against the large vol. change of alloy electrodes, as evidenced by both electrochem. measurement and at. force microscopy.  Our work unravels the causes for the superiority of ether-based electrolytes in sodium-ion batteries, and we expect the potential of such an optimized SEI to enable the application of high-capacity anodes such as microsized alloys.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoO-t0XJX45m7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg7pE_C5FhcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXntFentb8%253D&amp;md5=abd0870fe93a073a14e53e297d749adb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.0c00148"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wahyudi, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cavallo, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Anthopoulos, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshareef, H.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of sodium and potassium ion batteries with greater energy d. is gaining great attention.  Although recently proposed alloying anodes (e.g., Sn and Bi) demonstrate much higher capacity than classic carbon anodes, their severe capacity fading hinders their practical applications.  The failure mechanism has traditionally been attributed to the large volumetric change and/or their fragile solid electrolyte interphase (SEI).  However, herein a completely new concept and approach are presented based on electrolyte engineering to stabilize alloying anodes.  This approach results in unprecedented high capacity (&gt; 650 mAh g-1) and stability (&gt; 500 cycles) of alloying anodes by simply tuning the electrolyte compns., without the need for nanostructural control and/or carbon modification.  It is confirmed that the cation solvation structure, particularly the type and location of the anions in the electrolyte, plays a crit. role in alloying anode stabilization.  A new anionic and alloying anode reaction model is presented showing that the root cause of the capacity fading in these alloys is dictated by the properties of the anions and not only the vol. change or fragile SEI effect.  Our model elucidates the failure mechanism in alloying anodes and provides a new guideline for electrolyte design that stabilizes alloying anodes in emerging mobile ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvlve8l8FFQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg7pE_C5FhcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisFWrtbg%253D&amp;md5=1aa8da1f21de6c9b41d98d19e371bb88</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.7b01398"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stratford, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The alloying mechanism of high-capacity tin anodes for sodium-ion batteries is investigated using a combined theor. and exptl. approach. Further reaction with sodium results in the formation of structures contg. Sn-Sn dumbbells, which interconvert through a solid-soln. mechanism.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A phase-field model, accounting for large elasto-plastic deformation, is developed to study the evolution of phase, morphol. and stress in cryst. silicon (Si) electrodes upon lithium (Li) insertion. The present phase-field model is validated in comparison with a non-linear concn.-dependent diffusion model of lithiation in Si electrodes.  It is shown that as the lithiation proceeds, the hoop stress changes from the initial compression to tension in the surface layer of the Si electrode, which may explain the surface cracking obsd. in expts.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithiation of individual silicon nanoparticles was studied in real time with in situ TEM.  A strong size dependence of fracture was discovered; i.e., there exists a crit. particle diam. of ∼150 nm, below which the particles neither cracked nor fractured upon 1st lithiation, and above which the particles initially formed surface cracks and then fractured due to lithiation-induced swelling.  The unexpected surface cracking arose owing to the buildup of large tensile hoop stress, which reversed the initial compression, in the surface layer.  The stress reversal was attributed to the unique mechanism of lithiation in cryst. Si, taking place by movement of a two-phase boundary between the inner core of pristine Si and the outer shell of amorphous Li-Si alloy.  While the resulting hoop tension tended to initiate surface cracks, the small-sized nanoparticles nevertheless averted fracture.  This is because the stored strain energy from electrochem. reactions was insufficient to drive crack propagation, as dictated by the interplay between the two length scales, i.e., particle diam. and crack size, that control the fracture.  These results are diametrically opposite to those obtained previously from single-phase modeling, which predicted only compressive hoop stress in the surface layer and thus crack initiation from the center in lithiated Si particles and wires.  The work provides direct evidence of the mech. robustness of small Si nanoparticles for applications in lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq7mT_29kDFu7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf3IfBfKOgiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivVWksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=7c5347ef8e51a00af47eb935de9a2176</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00690J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sha, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sn Nanoparticles@Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofiber Composites as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted increasing attention as an important supplement or alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs) due to the abundance of sodium resources and its much lower cost.  A crit. issue and great challenge in current battery research for the extensive application of SIBs is the development of earth-abundant and high-performance electrode materials.  In various studies of these electrode materials, Sn-based nanocomposites have been identified as promising anodes for SIBs.  In this study, Sn nanoparticles on nitrogen-doped carbon nanofiber composites (Sn@NCNFs) have been synthesized by an electrostatic spinning technique and used as anodes for SIBs.  Morphol. and structural characterizations indicate that the Sn nanoparticles adhere uniformly on the surface of the nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers.  The corresponding specific capacity can reach over 600 mA h g-1 at 0.1C after 200 cycles.  Addnl., these Sn@NCNFs also show excellent high-rate cycling performance and can maintain a capacity of up to 390 mA h g-1 even at an extremely high rate of 1C for over 1000 cycles.  The results demonstrate that this Sn@NCNFs composite is a promising anode material with good reversible capacity and cycling performance for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq5eV_z-chx-bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf3IfBfKOgiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjslSms74%253D&amp;md5=7c42698b0ca5c27ece5151f5c8b153bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.03.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Highly Stable (SnO<sub>x</sub>-Sn)@Few Layered Graphene Composite Anode of Sodium-Ion Batteries Synthesized by Oxygen Plasma Assisted Milling</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly stable (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene composite anode of sodium-ion batteries synthesized by oxygen plasma assisted milling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Deliang; Liu, Jiangwen; Li, Xiang; Hu, Renzong; Zeng, Meiqing; Yang, Lichun; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene ((SnOx-Sn)@FLG) composite has been synthesized by O plasma-assisted milling.  Owing to the synergistic effect of rapid plasma heating and ball mill grinding, SnOx (1≤ x ≤2) nanoparticles generated from the reaction of Sn with O are tightly wrapped by FLG nanosheets which are simultaneously exfoliated from expanded graphite, forming secondary micro granules.  Inside the granules, the small size of the SnOx nanoparticles enables the fast kinetics for Na+ transfer.  The in-situ formed FLG and residual Sn nanoparticles improve the elec. cond. of the composite, meanwhile alleviate the aggregation of SnOx nanoparticles and relieve the vol. change during the cycling, which is beneficial for the cyclic stability for the Na+ storage.  As an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 448 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g in the 1st cycle, with 82.6% capacity retention after 250 cycles.  Even when the c.d. increases to 1000 mA/g, this composite retains 316.5 mAh/g after 250 cycles.  With superior Na+ storage stability, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite can be a promising anode material for high performance sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpu3VJ7Z_IUi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf3IfBfKOgiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkslyjtrY%253D&amp;md5=411e9333c9fa824c27eb67deca3362e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf3IfBfKOgiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVKksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf146b366c93613b170938edd33ec0fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01480E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ying, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, W.-Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall Sn Nanodots Embedded inside N-Doped Carbon Microcages as High-Performance Lithium and Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchin-like CoSe2 assembled by nanorods was synthesized via simple solvothermal route and was 1st applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with ether-based electrolytes. During the charge process, Co 1st reacts with Na2Se to form NaxCoSe2 and then turns back to CoSe2.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering that the high capacity, long-term cycle life, and high-rate capability of anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a bottleneck currently, a series of Co-doped FeS2 solid solns. with different Co contents were prepd. by a facile solvothermal method, and for the first time their Na-storage properties were investigated. The redox reactions of NaxCo0.5Fe0.5S2 are dominated by pseudocapacitive behavior, leading to fast Na+ insertion/extn. and durable cycle life.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible power sources showed great promise in next-generation bendable, implantable, and wearable electronic systems.  Here, flexible and binder-free electrodes of Na3V2(PO4)3/reduced graphene oxide (NVP/rGO) and Sb/rGO nanocomposites for Na-ion batteries are reported.  The Sb/rGO and NVP/rGO paper electrodes with high flexibility and tailorability can be easily fabricated.  Sb and NVP nanoparticles are embedded homogeneously in the interconnected framework of rGO nanosheets, which provides structurally stable hosts for Na-ion intercalation and deintercalation.  The NVP/rGO paper-like cathode delivers a reversible capacity of 113 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and high capacity retention of ≈96.6% after 120 cycles.  The Sb/rGO paper-like anode gives a highly reversible capacity of 612 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, an excellent rate capacity up to 30 C, and a good cycle performance.  Also, the Na-ion full cell of NVP/rGO//Sb/rGO was fabricated, delivering a highly reversible capacity of ≈400 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 charge/discharge cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, double-walled cryst. Sb@amorphous TiO2-x nanotubes are synthesized by the calcination of Sb2S3@TiO2 nanorods in Ar/H2 produced by the hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate (TBOT) on Sb2S3 nanorods.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antinomy has received considerable attention as one of the most promising anode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity and suitable working voltage.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene incorporation should be one effective strategy to develop advanced electrode materials for a sodium-ion battery (SIB).  Herein, the micro/nanostructural Sb/graphene composite (Sb-O-G) is successfully prepd. with the uniform Sb nanospheres (∼100 nm) bound on the graphene via oxygen bonds.  It is revealed that the in-situ-constructed oxygen bonds play a significant role on enhancing Na-storage properties, esp. the ultrafast charge/discharge capability.  The oxygen-bond-enhanced Sb-O-G composite can deliver a high capacity of 220 mAh/g at an ultrahigh c.d. of 12 A/g, which is obviously superior to the similar Sb/G composite (130 mAh/g at 10 A/g) just without Sb-O-C bonds.  It also exhibits the highest Na-storage capacity compared to Sb/G and pure Sb nanoparticles as well as the best cycling performance.  More importantly, this Sb-O-G anode achieves ultrafast (120 C) energy storage in SIB full cells, which have already been shown to power a 26-bulb array and calculator.  All of these superior performances originate from the structural stability of Sb-O-C bonds during Na uptake/release, which has been verified by ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopies and IR spectroscopies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAWqDAYuZl6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgy_dvQqbIyPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjvFylur8%253D&amp;md5=20ff4444ec296955ad0cbb06a02dfbef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201904771"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bu, X. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Nanoparticle@Carbon Composite Anodes for Ultralong Cycle Life and High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>31</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1904771</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201904771</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth Nanoparticle@Carbon Composite Anodes for Ultralong Cycle Life and High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Peixun; Bai, Panxing; Li, Ang; Li, Benfang; Cheng, Mingren; Chen, Yiping; Huang, Shuping; Jiang, Qiang; Bu, Xian-He; Xu, Yunhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1904771</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi has emerged as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), owing to its high capacity and suitable operating potential.  However, large vol. changes during alloying/dealloying processes lead to poor cycling performance.  Here, Bi nanoparticle@C (Bi@C) composite is prepd. via a facile annealing method using a com. coordination compd. precursor of Bi citrate.  The composite has a uniform structure with Bi nanoparticles embedded within a C framework.  The nanosized structure ensures a fast kinetics and efficient alleviation of stress/strain caused by the vol. change, and the resilient and conductive C matrix provides an interconnected electron transportation pathway.  The Bi@C composite delivers outstanding Na-storage performance with an ultralong cycle life of 30,000 cycles at a high c.d. of 8 A/g and an excellent rate capability of 71% capacity retention at an ultrahigh current rate of 60 A/g.  Even at a high mass loading of 11.5 mg/cm2, a stable reversible capacity of 280 mAh/g can be obtained after 200 cycles.  Full SIBs by pairing with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode demonstrates superior performance.  Combining the facile synthesis and the com. precursor, the exceptional performance makes the Bi@C composite very promising for practical large-scale applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphFbJVR5Fy-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgy_dvQqbIyPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFaks7zJ&amp;md5=2ab88019326b5ea2f446f861c305a41d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b00818"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface Modification of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> by Nitrogen and Sulfur Dual-Doped Carbon Layer with Advanced Sodium Storage Property</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13151</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13162</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.7b00818</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface Modification of Na3V2(PO4)3 by Nitrogen and Sulfur Dual-Doped Carbon Layer with Advanced Sodium Storage Property</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Xinghui; Ou, Xing; Zheng, Fenghua; Pan, Qichang; Xiong, Xunhui; Hu, Renzong; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13151-13162</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped carbon layer wrapped Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles (NVP@NSC) have been successfully fabricated by the facile solid-state method.  In this hierarchical structure, the Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles are well dispersed and closely coated by nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped carbon layer, constructing an effective and interconnected conducting network to reduce the internal resistance.  Furthermore, the uniform coating layers alleviate the agglomeration of Na3V2(PO4)3 as well as mitigate the side reaction between electrode and electrolyte.  Because of the excellent electron transfer mutually enhancing sodium diffusion for this extraordinary structure, the NVP@NSC composite delivers an impressive discharge capacity of 113.0 mAh g-1 at 1 C and shows a capacity retention of 82.1% after 5000 cycles at an ultrahigh rate of 50 C, suggesting the remarkable rate capability and long cyclicity.  Surprisingly, a reversible capacity of 91.1 mAh g-1 is maintained after 1000 cycles at 5 C under the elevated temp. of 55 °C.  The approach of nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 provides an effective and promising strategy to enhance the ultrahigh rate and ultralong life property of cathode, which can be used for large-scale com. prodn. in sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0gNMT4Ra6KrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgy_dvQqbIyPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXltVSkt7g%253D&amp;md5=0df9650b3f37a70feb1012492856807f</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes2"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i2">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c00489?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c00489</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD patterns and SEM images of commercial μ-Sn and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C. Voltage vs capacity profiles of μ-Sn in different voltage windows in the 40th cycle and in the 121st cycle. EIS spectra of μ-Sn at different voltage plateaus. Electrochemical performances of μ-Bi in PIBs. Parameters used in DFT calculations and ANSYS simulations (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c00489/suppl_file/nl1c00489_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c00489/suppl_file/nl1c00489_si_001.pdf">nl1c00489_si_001.pdf (0.99 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

<script nonce="90da85e18cf1b325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da85e18cf1b325-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera
